Reference leaks were reported in issues such as CUDA memory leaks with torch.compile in both stable and trunk versions, as well as memory leaks in torch.compile after aborting backward.\n\n## Reference Cycles and GPU Memory\n\nReference cycles in Python code happen frequently and can cause GPU tensors to accumulate over time and then be released only during automatic garbage collection. CPython's garbage collection frees unreachable objects held in reference cycles via mark-and-sweep.\n\n## Solutions and Tools\n\nIt's best to avoid creating reference cycles in the first place. PyTorch has created a Reference Cycle Detector tool to find reference cycles keeping GPU tensors alive, which issues warnings every time the cycle collector runs and finds a CUDA tensor that gets freed, providing an object graph showing how the reference cycle refers to the GPU tensor.\n\n## Dynamo-Specific Graph Cleanup\n\nIn PyTorch's Dynamo implementation, the code calls `cleanup_graph()` and uses nn.Module \"proxies\" to prevent strong reference cycles where Dynamo created code holds onto references to modules that also have Dynamo code cache invalidation checks, which will delete the proxies when cache invalidation runs.\n\n## Reported Issues\n\nUsers have reported more than 10GB of memory leaked as a result of torch.compile with no obvious way of being cleaned.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_013X5WXZJrHkieMqYPyFcW5r","session_id":"784fa8d0-8a15-4b23-a661-a29c989bfcac","uuid":"400d647a-ad0d-49c2-b8e3-d123423d8809"}

Symbolic sizes are allocated for tensors on entry, based on policy decisions.\n\n## FakeTensorMode and ShapeEnv Relationship\n\nEvery FakeTensorMode contains a ShapeEnv, which tracks all symbolic shapes information, and their lifetimes are typically tied: they live and die together. Fake tensors are implemented as a tensor subclass, which means almost all of its implementation lives in Python!\n\n## Key Design Characteristics\n\nShapeEnv keeps track of symbolic shapes state when compiling a frame in Dynamo and is attached to FakeTensorMode. There is no ShapeEnv in C++; for ease of debugging, the entire symbolic reasoning apparatus is in Python.\n\n## Symbolic Shape Propagation\n\nThe system propagates symbolic sizes through operators, maintaining both FX IR so that faithful export of symbolic compute is possible, and Sympy expressions representing the size vars for reasoning about them. Because FakeTensorMode has a ShapeEnv (but meta implementations do not), meta functions that are data-dependent and require allocating an unbacked SymInt live in fake tensor, and fake tensor also takes care of memoizing unbacked SymInts.\n\n## Guards and Dynamic Shapes\n\nWhen done tracing and optimizing, all accumulated guards are installed with the compiled code; the compiled code is only reusable if all the guards evaluate true.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_013X5WXZJrHkieMqYPyFcW5r","session_id":"784fa8d0-8a15-4b23-a661-a29c989bfcac","uuid":"03d9393d-6b79-4a4b-beb0-aff949276729"}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01MGrVGmxq8gjCW7bVP5pU6X","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: (dynamic_shapes_core_concepts)=\\n2: # Dynamic Shapes Core Concepts\\n3: \\n4: This section described the core concepts of dynamic shapes in PyTorch. It is intended to be a\\n5: reference for engineers working on the PyTorch compiler stack and anyone who wants to understand\\n6: the inner workings of dynamic shapes.\\n7: \\n8: ## Symbolic integers\\n9: Symbolic integers (Symints) are used to represent variables that can span a range. For example:\\n10: ```python\\n11: x = torch.randn(5, 5) # this tensor has a shape [5, 5]\\n12: torch._dynamo.decorators.mark_dynamic(x, 0)\\n13: x = torch.randn(5, 5) # this tensor has a shape [s0, 5]\\n14: y = torch.cat([x, x], dim=0) # this tensor has a shape [2*s0, 5]\\n15: ```\\n16: \\n17: However, `z = x * y` would throw an error since we know that pointwise operation like multiply must\\n18: operate on same sized tensors but we know statically `s0 != 2 * s0`. Astute readers may point out\\n19: that this is not true when `s0 == 0` and the reason why that doesn't matter here is described in\\n20: {ref}`zero-one-specialization`.\\n21: \\n22: ## Guards\\n23: \\n24: In `torch.compile`, a guard is a mechanism that is used to ensure the validity of a compiled code graph.\\n25: By default, when you make a variable dynamic, it can range from `[-inf, inf]`. For example:\\n26: \\n27: ```python\\n28: def foo(x): return x / 2\\n29: \\n30: This works for any dynamic x. But if your code is:\\n31: \\n32: def foo(x)\\n33:     if x > 5:\\n34:         return x / 2\\n35:     return x / 3\\n36: ```\\n37: If you call `foo(6)`, it returns `x / 2` and adds a guard `x > 5`. Calling `foo(4)` later will\\n38: require recompilation because the guard is broken.\\n39: \\n40: ## Runtime Asserts\\n41: You can use runtime asserts to provide hints when you know certain facts, like batch size being less than 100:\\n42: \\n43: ```python\\n44: def foo(batch_size):\\n45:     torch._check(batch_size < 100)\\n46:     if batch_size < 100:\\n47:         return do_something\\n48:     return do_something_else()\\n49: ```\\n50: \\n51: ## \\\"Hint\\\" Value\\n52: \\n53: A \\\"hint value\\\" in the context of `torch.compile` refers to the actual values known during the compilation process that help the JIT compiler make decisions about expressions. Hint values are particularly useful for handling dynamic shapes, as they provide concrete information that guides the compilation without requiring recompilation for varying dimensions.\\n54: \\n55: \\n56: ## Dynamic Behavior Overview\\n57: \\n58: PyTorch assumes static shapes by default. When a size change is detected, it attempts to\\n59: recompile with dynamic input, although this may fail if there are conditional branches\\n60: or missing support for dynamic shapes. To diagnose overspecialization, you can set\\n61: `TORCH_LOGS=dynamic` to view \\\"eval\\\" entries that indicate when and why guards are added.\\n62: \\n63: If you anticipate a dimension will be dynamic, you can use `torch._dynamo.mark_dynamic(tensor, dim)`\\n64: to mark it in advance, specifying `min` and `max` values if known. Using `torch.compile(dynamic=False)`\\n65: disables automatic dynamic shapes, leading to recompilation for each unique size. Conversely,\\n66: `torch.compile(dynamic=True)` aims to use dynamic shapes as much as possible which is most useful\\n67: for small and may not be suitable for large models due to potential crashes or performance issues.\\n68: \\n69: You can whitelist specific sources to be marked as dynamic using the `TORCH_COMPILE_DYNAMIC_SOURCES` environment variable or `torch.compiler.config.dynamic_sources`. This is particularly useful for large\\n70: models with graph breaks, as you can maintain dynamism across graph breaks since\\n71: source names stay consistent. You can also use this to mark integers as dynamic. The format is a comma-delimited list of source names, for example, `\\\"L['x'], L['y']\\\"`.\\n72: You can also use regexes, for example, `\\\"L\\\\['x.*'\\\\], L\\\\['y.*'\\\\]\\\")`.\\n73: This whitelist takes precedence over other flags like `dynamic=False` `force_nn_module_property_static_shapes`, and `force_parameter_static_shapes`.\\n74: \\n75: Sometimes it can be cumbersome to find the right inputs to mark as dynamic. If\\n76: you're willing to take a performance hit for the first batch, one other affordable\\n77: option we have are the `eager_then_compile` stances which derive dynamism for you.\\n78: See {func}`torch.compiler.set_stance` for more details.\\n79: \\n80: \\n81: ## Overall Architecture\\n82: \\n83: Symbolic shapes workflow:\\n84: \\n85: 1. When compiling a frame in Dynamo, we allocate a `ShapeEnv` (attached to `FakeTensorMode`) to\\n86: track symbolic shapes.\\n87: 2. We allocate symbolic sizes for tensors on entry, based on policy decisions.\\n88: 3. We propagate symbolic sizes through operators, maintaining both FX IR for symbolic compute export\\n89: and Sympy expressions for reasoning.\\n90: 4. We add guards based on conditionals during Dynamo tracing or Inductor optimization, induced from both Python and C++.\\n91: 5. Guards can simplify symbolic variables. For instance, asserting `s0 == 4` allows replacing all occurrences of `s0` with `4`.\\n92: 6. After tracing and optimizing, we install all guards with the compiled code, ensuring reusability only if all guards evaluate true.\\n93: \\n94: ## Internal API Class Hierarchy\\n95: \\n96: ### Python Classes\\n97: \\n98: - **`SymInt`/`SymFloat`/`SymBool`**: User-visible classes that simulate their `int`/`float`/`bool` counterparts. Adding two `SymInts` produces a new `SymInt` that symbolically tracks the integer addition.\\n99: \\n100: - **`SymNode`**: Internal structure (accessible via `symint.node`) that holds actual symbolic tracking information. `SymNode` is type-erased, making it convenient to represent mixed-type operations.\\n101: \\n102: - **`ShapeEnv`**: Per-compile context state that tracks all free symbols and guards accumulated so far. Every `SymNode` records its `ShapeEnv` (but not vice versa; `SymNodes` are only used if they participate in a guard).\\n103: \\n104: ### C++ Equivalents\\n105: \\n106: - **`c10::SymInt`/`SymFloat`/`SymBool`**: User-visible classes that simulate `int`/`float`/`bool`\\n107: - **`c10::SymNode`/`SymNodeImpl`**: Analogous to Python `SymNode`\\n108: - **No C++ `ShapeEnv`**: For debugging ease, the entire symbolic reasoning apparatus remains in Python\\n109: \\n110: When writing code traceable with `make_fx`, it must handle `SymInt`/`SymFloat`/`SymBool` flowing through it.\\n111: \\n112: ## Value Ranges and Constraints\\n113: \\n114: Symbolic variables maintain **value ranges** that specify the set of possible values. By default:\\n115: - Size-like unbacked `SymInts` have value range `[0, Inf]`\\n116: - Regular unbacked `SymInts` have value range `[-Inf, Inf]`\\n117: \\n118: When assertions are made (e.g., `torch._check(x == y)`), the system:\\n119: 1. Attempts to replace unbacked symbols with equivalent expressions\\n120: 2. Refines value ranges based on the assertion\\n121: 3. Remembers boolean expressions that are always true\\n122: \\n123: Important files:\\n124: \\n125: - C++ SymInt API: `c10/core/SymInt.h`, `SymFloat.h`, `SymBool.h`\\n126: - Python SymInt API: `torch/__init__.py` (look for `SymInt/SymFloat/SymBool`)\\n127: - C++ plumbing: `c10/core/SymNodeImpl.h`, `torch/csrc/utils/python_symnode.h`, `torch/csrc/jit/python/init.cpp`\\n128: - Python infrastructure: `torch/fx/experimental/symbolic_shapes.py`\\n129: - Other important files: `torch/_subclasses/fake_tensor.py`, `torch/_meta_registrations.py`, decomps, PrimTorch refs\\n130: \\n131: ```{seealso}\\n132: * {ref}`dynamic_shapes`\\n133: * {ref}`dynamic_shapes_troubleshooting`\\n134: ```\\n135: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch@fabf73ad3b7f084b5f87a95236384a6b19e7834e/-/blob/docs/source/user_guide/torch_compiler/compile/dynamic_shapes_core_concepts.md%3FL1-150\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_013X5WXZJrHkieMqYPyFcW5r","session_id":"784fa8d0-8a15-4b23-a661-a29c989bfcac","uuid":"ee009491-10ad-4ddb-8126-7f58794ed81c"}

Dynamo Tracer Failure Handling\n\n**File: `/torch/_dynamo/convert_frame.py` (lines 862-876)**\n\nWhen the tracer encounters an exception during frame tracing, the failure handling works as follows:\n\n```python\ntry:\n    run_tracer()\n    tracer_output = DynamoTracerOutput(tracer)\n    output = tracer_output.output_graph\n    assert output is not None\n    # ... processing continues ...\nexcept Exception as e:\n    e._torch_dynamo_tracer_output = DynamoTracerOutput(tracer, error=True)\n    raise\n```\n\n**Key Points:**\n- When an exception occurs, a `DynamoTracerOutput` is created with `error=True` flag\n- This output is attached to the exception as `_torch_dynamo_tracer_output` attribute\n- The exception is re-raised so it can be caught at higher levels\n\n**At Higher Levels: `/torch/_dynamo/convert_frame.py` (lines 1419-1422, 1439-1442)**\n\n```python\nexcept exc.RestartAnalysis as e:\n    # Clean up the failed tracer output's graph to break reference cycles\n    failed_tracer_output = getattr(e, \"_torch_dynamo_tracer_output\", None)\n    if failed_tracer_output:\n        failed_tracer_output._cleanup_output_graph()\n```\n\nWhen `RestartAnalysis` or `SkipFrame` exceptions are caught, the cleanup method is explicitly called on the attached tracer output.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Graph Creation and Cleanup Architecture\n\n**File: `/torch/_dynamo/output_graph.py` (lines 3057-3090)**\n\nThe `DynamoTracerOutput` class maintains two graph references:\n\n```python\nclass DynamoTracerOutput:\n    error_on_graph_break: bool\n    is_tracing_resume_prologue: bool\n    output_graph: Optional[OutputGraph]\n    # output_graph_for_cleanup is set even when there's an error, to allow\n    # cleanup of graph nodes to break reference cycles\n    output_graph_for_cleanup: Optional[OutputGraph]\n    closure: Optional[tuple[Any, ...]]\n    f_globals: dict[str, Any]\n\n    def __init__(self, tracer: \"InstructionTranslatorBase\", error: Optional[Any] = None) -> None:\n        self.error_on_graph_break = tracer.error_on_graph_break\n        self.is_tracing_resume_prologue = tracer.is_tracing_resume_prologue\n        self.closure = tracer.closure\n        self.f_globals = tracer.f_globals\n        self.output_graph_for_cleanup = tracer.output\n        if error:\n            self.output_graph = None\n        else:\n            self.output_graph = tracer.output\n\n    def _cleanup_output_graph(self) -> None:\n        output_graph = self.output_graph_for_cleanup\n        if output_graph:\n            for tracer in output_graph.tracers:\n                tracer.graph._clear_nodes()\n            # Also clear tracked_fakes to break FakeTensorMode → ShapeEnv → TrackedFake → FakeTensor cycle\n            if (\n                output_graph.tracing_context.fake_mode\n                and output_graph.tracing_context.fake_mode.shape_env\n            ):\n                output_graph.tracing_context.fake_mode.shape_env.tracked_fakes = None\n```\n\n**Key Design Points:**\n\n1. **Two Output Graph References**: \n   - `output_graph`: Set only on successful tracing\n   - `output_graph_for_cleanup`: Set even when errors occur\n\n2. **Cleanup Process**:\n   - Clears all nodes from all SubgraphTracers\n   - Breaks reference cycles by clearing `tracked_fakes` in ShapeEnv\n\n3. **OutputGraph.cleanup() method** (lines 2980-3005):\n```python\ndef cleanup(self) -> None:\n    # There is a reference cycle between tracer and OutputGraph, causing\n    # some of the tensor objects to be held alive for longer than necessary.\n    self.root_tx = None\n    self.nn_modules.clear()\n    self.used_inlined_inbuilt_modules_names.clear()\n    self.param_name_to_source = None\n\n    for node in self.graph.nodes:\n        if \"grapharg\" in node.meta:\n            del node.meta[\"grapharg\"]\n    self.real_value_cache.clear()\n    self.input_name_to_proxy.clear()\n    self.side_effects.clear()\n    self.variable_tracker_cache.clear()\n    self.mro_source_cache.clear()\n    self.guarded_mro_absent_keys.clear()\n    self.signature_cache.clear()\n    self.register_finalizer_fns.clear()\n    self.dynamo_flat_name_to_original_fqn.clear()\n    self.tracing_context.clear()\n    self.input_source_to_var.clear()\n    self.leaf_var_creation_order.clear()\n    self.unspec_variable_map.clear()\n    self.backward_state.clear()\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. FakeTensorMode and ShapeEnv Interaction\n\n**File: `/torch/_dynamo/output_graph.py` (lines 663-691)**\n\nThe relationship between FakeTensorMode and ShapeEnv is established during OutputGraph initialization:\n\n```python\n# tracked_fakes says where any tensor that was wrapped to fake came\n# from.  It is similar to GraphArg, in that all GraphArgs will get\n# will get added to TrackedFakes, but TrackedFakes also contains\n# GraphArgs that got pruned, and things like Tensor attributes which\n# aren't explicit graph inputs.  Used by shape guard\nself.tracked_fakes: list[TrackedFake] = []\n\nshape_env = ShapeEnv(\n    # Reference Cycle!\n    # Share a reference to the list of TrackedFake.\n    #\n    # ShapeEnv needs this in order to be able to reproduce the call\n    # to produce_guards at an arbitrary time point. That is because\n    # TrackedFake instances may have its metadata changed throughout\n    # the program execution.\n    tracked_fakes=self.tracked_fakes,\n    # We want to allow capture scalar outputs and allow_dynamic_output_shape_ops when fullgraph=True\n    allow_scalar_outputs=one_graph or config.capture_scalar_outputs,\n    allow_dynamic_output_shape_ops=one_graph or config.capture_dynamic_output_shape_ops,\n    prefer_deferred_runtime_asserts_over_guards=config.prefer_deferred_runtime_asserts_over_guards,\n    co_fields=self.co_fields,\n)\n\n# In export mode, we force the shape_env to strictly disallow any constraining\n# of the user marked dynamic dims\nimport torch._functorch.config as _config\n\nwith _config.patch(fake_tensor_allow_unsafe_data_ptr_access=False):\n    fake_mode = torch._subclasses.FakeTensorMode(\n        shape_env=shape_env,\n        # TODO (tmanlaibaatar) Remove this once we always lift params and buffers\n        allow_non_fake_inputs=bool(self.export),\n        export=self.export,\n    )\nself.tracing_context: TracingContext = TracingContext(fake_mode)\n```\n\n**File: `/torch/_subclasses/fake_tensor.py` (lines 1250-1290)**\n\n```python\nclass FakeTensorMode(TorchDispatchMode):\n    cache: dict[_DispatchCacheKey, _DispatchCacheEntry] = {}\n    cache_hits: int = 0\n    cache_misses: int = 0\n    cache_bypasses: dict[str, int] = defaultdict(int)\n    # Every time you retrace using the same fake tensor mode, you should\n    # advance the epoch so we don't reuse unbacked memos\n    epoch: int = 0\n    in_kernel_invocation: bool = False\n    static_shapes: bool\n    shape_env: Optional[ShapeEnv]\n    # ... other attributes ...\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        *,\n        allow_fallback_kernels: bool = True,\n        allow_non_fake_inputs: bool = False,\n        shape_env: Optional[ShapeEnv] = None,\n        static_shapes: Optional[bool] = None,\n        # ...\n    ):\n```\n\n**File: `/torch/fx/experimental/symbolic_shapes.py` (lines 3730-3798)**\n\n```python\nclass ShapeEnv:\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        *,\n        should_record_events: Optional[bool] = None,\n        tracked_fakes: Optional[list[Any]] = None,\n        **kwargs: Any,\n    ) -> None:\n        self._init(**kwargs)\n        # ...\n        \n        # Keep track of the list of tracked fakes.\n        self.tracked_fakes = tracked_fakes\n        \n        # List of events for reconstructing ShapeEnv at arbitrary points in time.\n        self.events: list[ShapeEnvEvent] = (\n            [ShapeEnvEvent(ShapeEnv, kwargs=kwargs)]\n            if self.should_record_events\n            else []\n        )\n\n        # FakeTensor per-ShapeEnv operation cache. This is used for caching\n        # operations that contain symbolic shapes which have guards on the\n        # ShapeEnv (so are ShapeEnv-dependent).\n        #\n        # NOTE: It's important that SymNodes in this cache have their ShapeEnv\n        # stripped otherwise you end up with cycles which can only be cleaned\n        # with the GC.\n        self.fake_tensor_cache: dict[...] = {}\n```\n\n**Key Architectural Points:**\n\n1. **Lifetime Coupling**: Every FakeTensorMode contains a ShapeEnv, and their lifetimes are typically tied—they live and die together\n2. **Shared Reference**: ShapeEnv holds a reference to the same `tracked_fakes` list maintained by OutputGraph\n3. **Purpose**: ShapeEnv needs `tracked_fakes` to reproduce guard production at arbitrary time points during symbolic tracing\n4. **Reference Cycle**: This creates an explicit reference cycle: `FakeTensorMode` → `ShapeEnv` → `tracked_fakes` list → `FakeTensor` objects\n\n---\n\n### 4. Reference Cycles That Need Breaking\n\n**The Main Reference Cycle:**\n\n`FakeTensorMode` → `ShapeEnv` → `TrackedFake` list → `FakeTensor` objects → back to `FakeTensorMode`\n\n**Breaking the Cycle (lines 3085-3090 in output_graph.py):**\n\n```python\n# Also clear tracked_fakes to break FakeTensorMode → ShapeEnv → TrackedFake → FakeTensor cycle\nif (\n    output_graph.tracing_context.fake_mode\n    and output_graph.tracing_context.fake_mode.shape_env\n):\n    output_graph.tracing_context.fake_mode.shape_env.tracked_fakes = None\n```\n\n**File: `/torch/_dynamo/output_graph.py` (lines 2980-3005)**\n\nAdditional reference cycles are broken in `OutputGraph.cleanup()`:\n- `root_tx` set to None (tracer reference)\n- `nn_modules` cleared\n- All caches cleared (`real_value_cache`, `input_name_to_proxy`, `side_effects`, etc.)\n- `tracing_context` cleared\n\n---\n\n### 5. Architecture Overview (from Documentation)\n\n**File: `/docs/source/user_guide/torch_compiler/compile/dynamic_shapes_core_concepts.md`**\n\nThe complete workflow:\n\n1. **Allocation**: When compiling a frame in Dynamo, a `ShapeEnv` is allocated and attached to `FakeTensorMode` to track symbolic shapes\n2. **Propagation**: Symbolic sizes are allocated for tensors on entry based on policy decisions\n3. **Symbolic Reasoning**: Symbolic sizes are propagated through operators, maintaining:\n   - FX IR for faithful export of symbolic compute\n   - Sympy expressions for symbolic reasoning about sizes\n4. **Guard Installation**: After tracing and optimizing, all accumulated guards are installed with the compiled code\n5. **Reusability**: Compiled code is only reusable if all guards evaluate true\n\n**Python vs C++:**\n- `ShapeEnv`: Python only (no C++ equivalent)\n- `SymInt`/`SymFloat`/`SymBool`: Both Python and C++\n- `SymNode`: Both Python and C++ equivalents\n- Entire symbolic reasoning apparatus is in Python for ease of debugging\n\n---\n\n### 6. Key Files Summary\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Content |\n|------|---------|-------------|\n| `/torch/_dynamo/output_graph.py` | Core output graph and tracer output | `DynamoTracerOutput`, `OutputGraph`, cleanup logic |\n| `/torch/_dynamo/convert_frame.py` | Frame conversion and exception handling | Tracer failure handling, cleanup calls on exceptions |\n| `/torch/_subclasses/fake_tensor.py` | FakeTensor implementation | `FakeTensorMode` class definition |\n| `/torch/fx/experimental/symbolic_shapes.py` | Symbolic shape tracking | `ShapeEnv` class, symbolic reasoning |\n| `/torch/_dynamo/exc.py` | Exception definitions | `TorchDynamoException`, tracer output attachment |\n| `/torch/_guards.py` | Tracing context | `TracingContext` class |\n\n---\n\n### 7. Critical Design Insights\n\n1. **Two-Phase Error Handling**: Failed tracer outputs are preserved (`output_graph_for_cleanup`) even when errors occur, allowing cleanup without needing the actual output graph\n\n2. **Deliberate Reference Cycles**: The design intentionally creates reference cycles because the architectural need for `ShapeEnv` to hold a reference to `tracked_fakes` list for guard reproduction is critical\n\n3. **Python-Only Symbolic Shapes**: Unlike most of PyTorch which is C++-first, the entire symbolic shapes apparatus is in Python for debugging convenience\n\n4. **Guard-Based Recompilation**: The compiled code is only reusable if all accumulated guards remain true; when guards fail, retracing occurs\n\n5. **Weak References for Subgraph Tracers**: SubgraphTracers use weak references to their parent OutputGraph to avoid circular references\n\n---\n\n### Sources:\n- [Dynamic Shapes Core Concepts — PyTorch documentation](https://docs.pytorch.org/docs/stable/user_guide/torch_compiler/compile/dynamic_shapes_core_concepts.html)\n- [Fake Tensor — PyTorch documentation](https://docs.pytorch.org/docs/stable/user_guide/torch_compiler/torch.compiler_fake_tensor.md)\n- [Fixing torch.compile Reference Leaks - PyTorch Developer Mailing List](https://dev-discuss.pytorch.org/t/fixing-torch-compile-reference-leaks-automatic-deletion-of-dynamo-code-objects/2197)\n- [Understanding GPU Memory 2: Finding and Removing Reference Cycles](https://pytorch.org/blog/understanding-gpu-memory-2/)\n- [torch.compile Troubleshooting — PyTorch documentation](https://docs.pytorch.org/docs/stable/torch.compiler_troubleshooting.html)"},{"type":"text","text":"agentId: aecefb2282bfd6dc2 (for resuming to continue this agent's work if needed)\n<usage>total_tokens: 59507\ntool_uses: 28\nduration_ms: 77671</usage>"}]}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"784fa8d0-8a15-4b23-a661-a29c989bfcac","uuid":"6bcd67e6-5020-4c46-8307-2fd5cb705e45","tool_use_result":{"status":"completed","prompt":"Search for information about PyTorch dynamo tracer, failed tracer outputs, graph cleanup, FakeTensorMode, and ShapeEnv in the PyTorch repository. Architecture Overview (from Documentation)\n\n**File: `/docs/source/user_guide/torch_compiler/compile/dynamic_shapes_core_concepts.md`**\n\nThe complete workflow:\n\n1. **Allocation**: When compiling a frame in Dynamo, a `ShapeEnv` is allocated and attached to `FakeTensorMode` to track symbolic shapes\n2. **Propagation**: Symbolic sizes are allocated for tensors on entry based on policy decisions\n3. **Symbolic Reasoning**: Symbolic sizes are propagated through operators, maintaining:\n   - FX IR for faithful export of symbolic compute\n   - Sympy expressions for symbolic reasoning about sizes\n4. **Guard Installation**: After tracing and optimizing, all accumulated guards are installed with the compiled code\n5. **Reusability**: Compiled code is only reusable if all guards evaluate true\n\n**Python vs C++:**\n- `ShapeEnv`: Python only (no C++ equivalent)\n- `SymInt`/`SymFloat`/`SymBool`: Both Python and C++\n- `SymNode`: Both Python and C++ equivalents\n- Entire symbolic reasoning apparatus is in Python for ease of debugging\n\n---\n\n### 6. Key Files Summary\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Content |\n|------|---------|-------------|\n| `/torch/_dynamo/output_graph.py` | Core output graph and tracer output | `DynamoTracerOutput`, `OutputGraph`, cleanup logic |\n| `/torch/_dynamo/convert_frame.py` | Frame conversion and exception handling | Tracer failure handling, cleanup calls on exceptions |\n| `/torch/_subclasses/fake_tensor.py` | FakeTensor implementation | `FakeTensorMode` class definition |\n| `/torch/fx/experimental/symbolic_shapes.py` | Symbolic shape tracking | `ShapeEnv` class, symbolic reasoning |\n| `/torch/_dynamo/exc.py` | Exception definitions | `TorchDynamoException`, tracer output attachment |\n| `/torch/_guards.py` | Tracing context | `TracingContext` class |\n\n---\n\n### 7. Critical Design Insights\n\n1. **Two-Phase Error Handling**: Failed tracer outputs are preserved (`output_graph_for_cleanup`) even when errors occur, allowing cleanup without needing the actual output graph\n\n2. **Deliberate Reference Cycles**: The design intentionally creates reference cycles because the architectural need for `ShapeEnv` to hold a reference to `tracked_fakes` list for guard reproduction is critical\n\n3. **Python-Only Symbolic Shapes**: Unlike most of PyTorch which is C++-first, the entire symbolic shapes apparatus is in Python for debugging convenience\n\n4. **Guard-Based Recompilation**: The compiled code is only reusable if all accumulated guards remain true; when guards fail, retracing occurs\n\n5. **Weak References for Subgraph Tracers**: SubgraphTracers use weak references to their parent OutputGraph to avoid circular references\n\n---\n\n### Sources:\n- [Dynamic Shapes Core Concepts — PyTorch documentation](https://docs.pytorch.org/docs/stable/user_guide/torch_compiler/compile/dynamic_shapes_core_concepts.html)\n- [Fake Tensor — PyTorch documentation](https://docs.pytorch.org/docs/stable/user_guide/torch_compiler/torch.compiler_fake_tensor.md)\n- [Fixing torch.compile Reference Leaks - PyTorch Developer Mailing List](https://dev-discuss.pytorch.org/t/fixing-torch-compile-reference-leaks-automatic-deletion-of-dynamo-code-objects/2197)\n- [Understanding GPU Memory 2: Finding and Removing Reference Cycles](https://pytorch.org/blog/understanding-gpu-memory-2/)\n- [torch.compile Troubleshooting — PyTorch documentation](https://docs.pytorch.org/docs/stable/torch.compiler_troubleshooting.html)"}],"totalDurationMs":77671,"totalTokens":59507,"totalToolUseCount":28,"usage":{"input_tokens":5,"cache_creation_input_tokens":528,"cache_read_input_tokens":55120,"output_tokens":3854,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":528,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}}}

This prevents the `torch.utils.swap_tensors()` function from operating on tensors that have weak references, particularly those held by `FakeTensor.fake_mode` objects with weakref caches.\n\n## Related Pull Requests\n\n**Primary Fix: PR #169642**\n- Takes a targeted approach by cleaning up reference cycles rather than forcing garbage collection\n- Addresses cycles in `torch.fx.graph.Graph` and `torch.fx.node.Node` structures that accumulate from failed compiles\n- Replaces problematic strong references with weakrefs in `TrackedFake` to eliminate cycles\n\n**Earlier Attempts: PR #168326 (Draft)**\n- Explored using weak references for `FakeTensor.fake_mode`\n- Abandoned due to breaking export and standalone compile functionality\n\n## Status\nThe issue was marked as closed/completed with the implementation of PR #169642, which manually clears reference cycles to avoid requiring explicit garbage collection calls."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01NCmCmwQJYrbt9KLvH3cBXs","session_id":"784fa8d0-8a15-4b23-a661-a29c989bfcac","uuid":"f1045dfe-3602-471b-a0e6-a134e877d698"}

Here's what it does:\n\n```python\ndef _clear_nodes(self) -> None:\n    for node in reversed(self.nodes):\n        node.meta.clear()\n        self.erase_node(node)\n```\n\n**Functionality:** This method iterates through all nodes in reverse order, clears the metadata dictionary for each node, and then removes it from the graph. Dynamo**: Dynamo keeps weakref to tensors when interpreting byte-code or creating guards, and `torch.utils.swap_tensors` will fail if there are weakref's to input tensors.\n\n2. **With Module.to()**: 41a56f7 introduced strict reference-count checks for tensors passed into `torch.utils.swap_tensors` (added in PyTorch v2.3.1), with checks still present in the latest stable release (v2.9.0).\n\nThe root cause is that `swap_tensors` performs a low-level operation that requires exclusive access to tensor implementations, which is incompatible with weak references being held elsewhere in the code.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown This particularly affects `FakeTensor.fake_mode` objects with weakref caches.\n\n**Affected Tests (6 failing test cases):**\n1. `test_type_before_parametrizations_swap_True`\n2. `test_caching_parametrization_swap_True`\n3. `test_caching_parametrization_with_transfer_parametrizations_and_params_swap_True`\n4. `test_errors_parametrized_tensor_parametrization_swap_True`\n5. `test_new_spectral_norm_forward_swap_True`\n6. `test_parametrization_same_training_mode_swap_True`\n\n---\n\n### PR #169642: The Complete Fix\n\n**Direct Link:** https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/pull/169642\n\n**Status:** Merged on December 12, 2025, and cherry-picked to release/2.10 branch\n\n#### Files Modified:\n\n1. **torch/fx/graph.py** - Added `_clear_nodes()` method\n2. **torch/_dynamo/output_graph.py** - Added `_cleanup_output_graph()` method\n\n#### Exact Code Changes:\n\n**`_clear_nodes()` method in `torch/fx/graph.py`:**\n```python\ndef _clear_nodes(self) -> None:\n    for node in reversed(self.nodes):\n        node.meta.clear()\n        self.erase_node(node)\n```\n\n**`_cleanup_output_graph()` method in `torch/_dynamo/output_graph.py`:**\n```python\ndef _cleanup_output_graph(self) -> None:\n    output_graph = self.output_graph_for_cleanup\n    if output_graph:\n        for tracer in output_graph.tracers:\n            tracer.graph._clear_nodes()\n        # Also clear tracked_fakes to break FakeTensorMode → ShapeEnv → \n        # TrackedFake → FakeTensor cycle\n        if (\n            output_graph.tracing_context.fake_mode\n            and output_graph.tracing_context.fake_mode.shape_env\n        ):\n            output_graph.tracing_context.fake_mode.shape_env.tracked_fakes = None\n```\n\n#### What These Changes Do:\n\n1. **`_clear_nodes()`** - Manually breaks reference cycles in graph nodes by:\n   - Iterating through all nodes in reverse order\n   - Clearing the metadata dictionary (`meta.clear()`) for each node\n   - Erasing each node from the graph using `erase_node()`\n\n2. **`_cleanup_output_graph()`** - Cleans up failed tracer outputs by:\n   - Clearing reference cycles in graph nodes using `_clear_nodes()`\n   - Breaking the circular reference: FakeTensorMode → ShapeEnv → TrackedFake → FakeTensor → FakeTensorMode\n   - Setting `tracked_fakes = None` to eliminate the cycle\n\n#### PR Commits (8 total):\n\n1. gc example values from graph node meta (7e3a32d)\n2.
